## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Chemical Reaction Kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the temporal evolution of a chemical species concentration governed by differential rate laws. The rate of change dA_dt typically depends nonlinearly on the instantaneous concentration A (reflecting reaction order and mechanism) and may include explicit time t dependence for non-isothermal, flow, or catalyst-deactivation scenarios.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular elementary reaction)
- Second-order bimolecular: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (collision-dependent dimerization or reaction)
- General reaction order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical rate law with adjustable order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to thermodynamic equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-accelerated reaction with depletion limit)
- Time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (non-isothermal or ramped reaction conditions)
- Power-law time modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (aging catalyst or reactor wall effects)
- Inhibited kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (product or impurity suppression of active sites)
- Consecutive reaction approximation: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (decay coupled with time-varying regeneration)
- Induction period model: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) (delayed reaction onset before acceleration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Autocatalytic behavior → Polynomial rate forms with sign change like A*(c-A), producing inflection points in concentration curves
- Reversible reaction equilibrium → Linear combination of forward and backward terms (c0*A + c1), driving derivative to zero at steady state
- Non-isothermal/time-varying conditions → Explicit time dependence multiplying concentration terms (e.g., exp(c*t)*A or t**c*A)
- Complex surface/heterogeneous catalysis → Fractional or rational concentration dependencies indicating adsorption-limited steps
- Induction/delayed onset → Rate modifiers that suppress initial change, modeled by terms like (1 - exp(-c*t)) or similar switching functions
- Stoichiometric constraint in closed systems → Derivative signs strictly constrained by mass balance, typically negative for reactants and zero at completion
- Catalyst deactivation/aging → Explicit negative time powers or decay factors reducing the effective rate constant over long durations

### Analysis of Candidates

The Ground Truth (GT) numerical expression is:
`-0.17495597007573369 * A**2 + 0.591324193355756 * sin(log(A + 1))`
This simplifies to the structural form: `k1 * A**2 + k2 * sin(log(A + 1))`, where `k1` and `k2` are free constants. We will test each candidate for exact algebraic equivalence to this structure by assigning appropriate values to free constants.

**Candidate 1:** `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)`
- Set `c1 = 0`, `c2 = 0`, `c5 = 1`, `c4 = 1`, `c6 = 0`.
- Expression becomes `c0*A**2 + c3*sin(log(A + 1))`. Matches GT structure exactly.
- **Verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)`
- Expands to `c0*A**2 + c1*A + c2 + c3*sin(...)`. Identical to Candidate 1.
- Set `c1 = 0`, `c2 = 0`, `c5 = 1`, `c4 = 1`, `c6 = 0`. Matches GT.
- **Verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** `(A*c0 + (A*c1 + 1)*(A**2*c2 + A*c3 + c4*sin(A + c5)))/(A*c1 + 1)`
- Contains `sin(A + c5)`. The argument is linear in `A`, not `log(A + 1)`. Basis functions do not match.
- **Verdict: [NO MATCH]**

= `A*(A^2*c0+A*c1+c2)/(A+c4) + c3*sin(c5*log(A*c6+1))`
